# Evaluation of Titanic Passenger list

Using the data from Kaggle.com, we will evaluate a sample of the Titanic
passengers list to try to understand if there are any variables about why one
passenger could survive while another would perish.

by Jason Carter
October 24, 2017


{% raw %}
### Imports  
%config InlineBackend.figure_format = 'retina'   ### Make it pretty on my Mac
%matplotlib inline

import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
import pylab as plt
from matplotlib.pyplot import *
from IPython.core.interactiveshell import InteractiveShell
InteractiveShell.ast_node_interactivity = "all"


### Reusabel Functions
def labelMax(ax, x_offset=-0.02, y_offset = 0.5):
    for p in ax.patches:
        b = p.get_bbox()
        val = "{:.2f}".format(b.y1 + b.y0)        
        ax.annotate(val, ((b.x0 + b.x1)/2 + x_offset, b.y1 + y_offset))
{% endraw %}

### Clean Up




{% raw %}
### Remove columns to streamline
del df['PassengerId']
del df['Cabin']
del df['Ticket']       
del df['Name']           

{% endraw %}


{% raw %}
        



{% endraw %}

Evaluating the information about the data we are missing a good bit of the ages.
Lets see if we can find any relationships in the data so we can find the best
way to back fill those data points.



{% raw %}
#### Age

fig, axes = plt.subplots(nrows=2, ncols=2,figsize=(15,15))

a1 = df.groupby(['Sex']).mean()['Age'].plot(
    kind='bar', 
    title='Passengers Mean Age by Gender', 
    color=['r','b'], 
    ax=axes[0,0]);      
labelMax(a1)

a2 = df.groupby(['Sex', 'Pclass']).mean()['Age'].plot(
    kind='bar', 
    title='Passengers Mean Age by Gender and Class', 
    color=['r','b'], 
    ax=axes[0,1]);       
labelMax(a2)

a3 = df.groupby(['Sex', 'Pclass','Embarked']).mean()['Age'].plot(
    kind='bar', 
    title='Passengers Mean Age by \nGender, Class and Point of Embarkation', 
    color=['r','b','y'], 
    ax=axes[1,0]);       
labelMax(a3)
{% endraw %}

    Through our charts we can see that ages of each sex differs greatly by
class.  Breaking those classifications down one step further we can find the
averages by when the passenger boarded which gives us even more detail.  Using
the embarkation point as a split helps us to get a better average of missing
ages.



{% raw %}
#Lets double check the Embark for NaN
df[df['Embarked'].isnull()]


#### Embark
a1 = df.groupby(['Embarked']).count()['Age'].plot(
    kind='bar', 
    title='Passengers Embarking by Gender', 
    color=['r','b','y']);      
labelMax(a1)


## Embark Missing Values with most prevelant
df.loc[df['Embarked'].isnull(),'Embarked'] = 'S'
{% endraw %}

{% raw %}
## Fill in empty ages with averages by sex and class and point of embarkation
df['Age_C'] = df['Age'].groupby([df['Sex'], df['Pclass'], df['Embarked']]).apply(lambda x: x.fillna(x.median()))
df['Age_C'] = df['Age_C'].astype(int)

## Fare, lets round these fares to whole dollars for ease of use
df['Fare'] = df['Fare'].astype(int)


{% endraw %}


{% raw %}
figure = plt.figure(figsize=(15,8))
a = plt.subplot(2, 2, 1)
a = plt.hist([df[df['Survived']==1]['Age_C'], 
         df[df['Survived']==0]['Age_C']], 
         stacked=True, 
         color = ['g','r'],
         bins = 30,
         label = ['Survived','Perished'], )
b = plt.xlabel('Age')
b = plt.ylabel('Number of passengers')
b = plt.legend()

a = plt.subplot(2, 2, 3)
a = plt.hist([df[df['Survived']==1]['Pclass'], 
         df[df['Survived']==0]['Pclass']], 
         stacked=True, 
         color = ['g','r'],
         label = ['Survived','Perished'], )

b = plt.xlabel('PClass')
b = plt.ylabel('Number of passengers')
b = plt.xticks(range(0,4) )
b = plt.legend()

### Fares
fig, axes = plt.subplots(figsize=(15,5))

### Get Rid of the outliers to clean it up a bit
df = df[np.abs(df['Fare']-df['Fare'].mean())<=(3*df['Fare'].std())]

a = df['Fare'].plot(kind='hist', bins=50)
b = a.set_xlim(xmin = 0)
b = plt.xlabel('Fare')
b = plt.ylabel('Number of passengers')

%matplotlib inline
fig, ax = subplots()
title = 'Scatter Plot of\n Survived vs Perished\n by Age/Fare'
sf_mean = df[df['Survived']==1]['Fare'].mean()
pf_mean = df[df['Survived']==0]['Fare'].mean()

a = df[df['Survived']==1].plot(kind='scatter', x='Fare', y='Age',  c='g', figsize=(8,8), ax=ax, title=title)
a = df[df['Survived']==0].plot(kind='scatter', x='Fare', y='Age',  c='r', figsize=(8,8), ax=ax)

b = a.axvline(sf_mean, color='green')  ### Show the Mean Fare for Survivors
b = a.axvline(pf_mean, color='red')    ### Show the Mean Fare for Death

b = ax.legend(['Mean Survival Fare - ${:.1f}'.format(sf_mean),
               'Mean Perished Fare - ${:.1f}'.format(pf_mean),
               'Survived',
               'Perished']
             )
